Page 15

Random Thoughts

Ma Rufei's Humor 272

— Zhan Lu

In the days leading up to the end of the lunar year, storytellers are always mobilized to hold large-scale storytelling events at various storytelling venues inside and outside the city. Among them, when talking about the elder Mr. Ma Rufei, those who tell short stories always give him a thumbs up, saying that he is the one and only leader in the storytelling world.

I was born too late to hear Ma Rufei's wonderful storytelling, but when I was a child, I heard Mr. Lao Dan, who had listened to Ma Rufei's storytelling, say that Ma Rufei's humorous arguments could be considered the Eastern Bernard Shaw. I occasionally recall them and briefly describe them below:

Ma Rufei met a stranger and asked each other's names. Ma said, "It's strange (奇哉)." Ma knew that the guest was joking, using the homophone for "strange (奇)" to mean "riding (騎)," which was a bit malicious. So he asked the guest, "Is your father healthy?" The guest said, "Still healthy." He asked again, "What about your mother?" The guest said, "Unfortunately, she is gone (失恃)." Ma repeatedly sighed and said, "How strange (奇煞哉)!" The guest could not help but feel embarrassed.

When Ma Rufei told stories, he had a great appeal. The storytelling venue was often crowded with people. The venue owner was greedy and forgot his righteousness, reporting fewer people and pocketing the rest of the money, which was called "eating heads." Ma knew about it, but pretended not to know. After finishing his storytelling, he stepped down from the stage and exchanged greetings with the venue owner. First, he asked the venue owner, "How is your health?" The venue owner said, "Thanks to you, still healthy (窮健)." Ma then asked, "How is your diet?" The venue owner said, "Two bowls per meal." Ma repeatedly urged, "Be careful when eating." The venue owner's face immediately became hot.

Ma Rufei had a temper. When the show had been going on for too long, he liked to cause some trouble and break up the show. When Ma was performing at Sanwanchang, he heard that there was a young man among the audience who was the son of someone from the Water Conservancy Bureau. He was specifically making trouble in the venue. Not only did the audience hate it, but Ma also despised him. One day, Ma was telling a joke in an interlude, briefly saying, "The Dragon King was lecturing on the Dragon Treasury True Scripture in the Crystal Palace. All the aquatic creatures had to enter the palace on time to listen to the lecture, or they would be refused entry. At that time, all the aquatic creatures reported in one by one, but the turtle walked slowly and missed the time. By the time it crawled to the Crystal Palace, the palace gate was already tightly closed. The turtle had no choice but to lie in the water and wait. After a while, the lecture was over, and the palace gate opened. The turtle then slowly walked up to the palace. The Dragon King scolded, "You turtle, why didn't you listen to the lecture?" The turtle said, "The little one was listening." The Dragon King said, "Where were you listening?" The turtle said, "The little one was listening in the water." When the interlude reached this point, the audience all laughed at the son of the Water Conservancy Bureau. The man was furious, waving his fists and sleeves, and broke up the show into chaos. The venue owner cried out in pain, but Ma Rufei was happy.

Madame Someone 273

— Yu Shan

Madame Someone, I forgot her last name. But she is always Madame Someone's, and the mother of Someone's five children.

Madame Someone's father was a genuine scholar, so Madame Someone received a "good" education from a young age.

Her father knew that "a woman's lack of talent is a virtue," so Madame Someone now only recognizes a few characters the size of watermelons. Her father knew that a woman should have "the four virtues of obedience," so he kept Madame Someone locked in her "boudoir" all day long, not allowing her to come out.

I don't remember the year Madame Someone arrived at Someone's house. Madame Someone herself doesn't remember either. However, Madame Someone has never argued with Someone since she arrived at his house, and she has given birth to five children, two girls and three boys, and there is one in her belly, and no one knows if it's a boy or a girl.

Although Madame Someone has not read many books, she recognizes a few characters, and these characters are all very practical for Madame Someone, like: the East, South, West, North, Middle, Fortune, Spring, Summer, Autumn, Winter, 1, 2, 3, ... 9 in "Mahjong." She is very familiar with what Fang Maolin, Tian Fusang, etc. are in the "Flower Club." Even with her eyes closed, she can think of: Tian is square, but Fang is not square. Not only that, she also knows that Fang Maolin is a monk, and Tian Fusang is a dog. Madame Someone knows the rest, but I only know these. If you want to know, you can ask Madame Someone.

Madame Someone's talent is like this. Madame Someone's ability is also great: she can take a four-year-old child, hold a two-year-old daughter, and carry a child that is already seven months in her belly to play "Mahjong." If you list her daily work on a table, you will be speechless after reading it.

"Get up at eight in the morning, first dress and wash the children, then wash yourself. After washing, prepare the noodle water with Sheng Sheng, it is already nine o'clock. Then take the four-year-old child and the two-year-old daughter to the small vegetable market to buy vegetables. When you get home, you cook rice and tidy up the room. After tidying up, cook vegetables. The children are clamoring to eat. After all the hard work of cooking, after eating, play "Bamboo City" with the neighbor's sister-in-law, the landlady across the street, and the teacher's wife in the attic, twelve rounds, twenty-four rounds, day and night. There is no time to cook dinner, so eat noodles."

Madame Someone's daily work is roughly like this. She doesn't need a maid. The reasons are: 1. Maids need money and food. 2. I am afraid that the maids will "skim" and report false accounts. 3. It's very annoying.

I haven't seen Madame Someone since the January 28th Incident. I don't know where she went.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 274

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Four

Drinking and Dining, Merry-Making Filled with Tears of Farewell

Burning the Midnight Oil, Sweet Dreams Murmuring Through the Long Night

Old Master Zhao, in the room across, heard his son laughing heartily, which he found quite puzzling. He stuck his head out of his doorway to look, only to see the curtain of the bridal chamber hanging low, and the sound inside had ceased. He thought to himself, young people are young people after all; such a new marriage followed by departure to join the army, no one can truly bear it. Yet they're still laughing and making merry in their confusion. After a long while, he finally heard the couple coming out together. It turned out they had agreed to go out and buy ingredients for making馅饼 [xiàn bǐng - stuffed pancakes]. As they walked to the front courtyard, their laughter still reached the back courtyard, so they must have been very happy indeed. Half an hour later, Ziqiang came in, his face still bearing a look of worry. Old Master Zhao asked, "Where have you been?" Ziqiang said, "She wanted to make stuffed pancakes for me to eat and insisted I go with her to buy the ingredients, so I had to accompany her. Actually, I don't really want to eat anything." As he spoke, he sat down lazily on a chair. Old Master Zhao said, "She seems very happy. Is it because you said you would bring her out to join you in the future?" Ziqiang pondered for a moment and said, "Maybe..." After speaking, he let out a long sigh. The curtain was lifted, and Guizhi skipped in with a smile, saying to Old Master Zhao, "Father, I'm making stuffed pancakes for you to eat, okay?" Old Master Zhao nodded. Guizhi smiled and said, "Ziqiang is leaving tomorrow, and I'm giving him a farewell feast. Can we have a little wine?" Old Master Zhao saw that she seemed truly happy, and said with a smile, "Logically, you can let him have a cup of farewell wine. But he has to catch the early bus tomorrow morning. If he drinks too much, he won't be able to get up." Guizhi smiled and said, "If he drinks at dinner tonight, he won't be able to wake up tomorrow morning? He'd have to drink a whole jar!" As she spoke, she gave Ziqiang a playful glance and said, "How much can you drink? We'll make a bet." After speaking, she went off with a laugh. Old Master Zhao, seeing her like this, was puzzled. Ziqiang laughed and said, "She's completely childish. She said she's going to sit with me and talk until dawn tonight." Old Master Zhao said, "Don't act like a child. When you get to Leizhou, you'll have to walk. The weather is getting colder. I imagine the area around the Great Wall is colder than here, right?" (242)

Insomnia 275

— Jin Zi

Because I am a person who cherishes life and fears death the most, whenever I feel a little unwell, I rush to the doctor. The first thing I always say is, "Doctor, will this ailment kill me?" As a result, not only have I not died so far, but also, because I sought treatment early, I haven't even suffered a major illness once.

But now, I have contracted a very pitiful ailment, which is the so-called "insomnia." Not long ago, I seem to have seen an article in a newspaper titled "City Sickness," which also mentioned "insomnia." Indeed, insomnia is a condition that is most likely to affect city dwellers because the causes of insomnia invariably boil down to love and economic issues. And city dwellers are constantly turning somersaults in these two areas all day long. So, how can you expect them not to suffer from insomnia!

However, the reason I suffer from insomnia is neither due to love nor economics, but because I have a few mixed-up small problems that are difficult to solve, and I unknowingly thought too much, leading to insomnia. But let's put aside the reasons for my insomnia for now and just talk about the situation after suffering from insomnia.

I don't know how I was awakened that night. The short hand on the clock hadn't even reached eleven o'clock, and yet my sleepiness had completely vanished. At first, I lay quietly, not paying much attention. After more than an hour, I still couldn't fall back asleep. I suddenly remembered what I had read in a book, so I silently counted one, two, three, four, five, six... Unexpectedly, the more I counted, the more awake I became, and I could barely stay in bed. So, I took a second step: I quickly got up, washed my feet with hot water until the skin on my feet turned completely red. I thought this would surely draw the blood away from my brain, so I quickly crawled back into bed. But it was no use. I tossed and turned until daybreak. The next day, I rushed to find a doctor. Unexpectedly, the doctor said, "There is no cure for insomnia, you can only restrain your thoughts." Oh dear! This is terrible!*

It may be possible to force a person not to eat delicacies and only eat plain rice. It may not even be too difficult to force him to keep his eyes closed all day and not look at anything. But it is absolutely impossible to force him not to think. At the time, I was very angry that the doctor didn't prescribe any medicine for me, especially because I feared that this incurable insomnia might end my life. So, I angrily went to buy a bottle of sleeping pills. But the clerk at the pharmacy had the best of intentions and repeatedly told me not to take them if possible. He wasn't afraid that I would commit suicide, but rather that I would become addicted. So, I can only not take them, and I am still struggling in the pain of insomnia.

Recently, he plans to establish a rural primary school in Wangcun, Wuxi, his hometown. After consultation, the great calligraphers and painters Chen Junmo, Huang Rui, Chen Zhangkuan, and Xu Yanqiu have agreed to hold a joint reduced-price sale. The proceeds from the sale will be donated to cover the school's operating expenses. Detailed regulations have been drawn up and can be obtained from the Shanghai Newspaper Office in Youxin Lane, Second Ma Road.

Little Time Table

Method for Making Preserved Meat and Dried Fish 276

— Ji Yu

It's the middle of winter, the time of the year for腊 [là, the twelfth lunar month] offerings. Residents can take advantage of this time to make some preserved meat and dried fish. If you make it after the start of spring, it will go bad. I remember one year when I had already passed the start of spring, my family salted a few hams. Who knew that by the time summer began, many small black worms had crawled out of the meat, and I didn't dare eat it after that. So, you must salt the meat in the twelfth lunar month.

First, let's talk about making preserved meat: Go to the butcher shop and choose several large hind legs (preferably pigs that eat bean cakes). Bring them back and put them in an open-mouthed jar. Put on a new straw sandal (you can also rub it with your hand, but it's very painful). Use a handful of salt and rub it hard on the skin, several times. Stop only when the skin of the meat starts to sweat. Then turn it over and rub the lean meat inside, also rubbing it a lot. Finally, rub the shanks and hooves. The amount of salt to use is ten to twelve ounces for a large leg of meat. You can't use too little. Once all the legs of meat are rubbed, place them flat in the jar and put several clean large stones on top to weigh them down. The next day, go to the butcher shop and ask for a small bowl of硝露 [xiāo lù - saltpetre solution] and pour it into the jar. After that, turn the meat over every day, rotating its position. After three weeks or so, take the meat out of the jar. Tie each piece with straw rope and hang it under the eaves to dry in the sun. In the evening, take it down and soak it in the jar, weighing it down with stones. Take it out the next day to dry again. After drying it in the sun for seven or eight days, hang the meat in a shady, windy place and let it dry naturally. If you dry it any longer, the meat will become tough. When bamboo shoots are in season, chop off a large piece and cook it with bamboo shoots. Or you can eat it in June. The taste is unmatched, because this preserved meat is really more delicious than ham and Nanjing spiced meat. It's both fresh and tender.

Now, let's talk about making dried fish: Around the 20th of the twelfth lunar month, buy a dozen catties of live large mackerel. Bring them back, slaughter them (do not wash them or remove the scales), remove the contents of the belly, and cut them in half (the head and tail should be cooked separately. Simmer the whole fish head with ham and 冬菇 [dōng gū - shiitake mushrooms] for an excellent taste, and the head also has a lot of brain). Cut them into sections, and lightly rub each section on both sides with salt. Place them in a large bowl or small jar, rubbing one section and then placing it in the jar. After all the sections are rubbed and arranged evenly, press a few small stones on the fish to keep them tightly packed together, leaving no gaps, or else the cats will steal them to eat. Around the middle of the first lunar month, take the fish out. Use thread for stitching shoe soles to string up each piece and hang them on a bamboo pole to dry in the sun for five or six days. Then hang them in a ventilated place. Around the tenth of the second lunar month, take the fish down, wash them clean, remove the scales, and cut them into squares (or leave them whole). Use a towel to absorb the moisture and dry them in the sun briefly. Take them in, put them in a large porcelain lion jar, pour in some 高梁 [gāo liáng - sorghum] wine. The amount of wine should almost cover the fish. At that time, you can also cut a few slices of preserved meat and put them in. Then buy some 酒酿 [jiǔ niàng - fermented glutinous rice] and spread it on top. The amount is up to you. If you want to add peppercorns to the fish, you can add eight or nine, but you don't have to. Then put the lid on and seal it with oilcloth on the outside. Around the time of the Dragon Boat Festival, take a few pieces and put them in a bowl, add some scallions, and steam them in the rice pot to eat? It really has a unique flavor. The fish is fragrant and tender and goes well with rice, no less than the dried fish sold in the market, and the price is much cheaper!

Shantou's Oyster Omelette 277

— Nai Chang

Shantou is close to the sea, and aquatic products are extremely abundant. Among these abundant aquatic products, oysters are one of the most famous. Those who gather oysters are mostly villagers near Shantou. Although they do not form large groups, they often accompany each other to chisel them from the rocks and the base pillars of the docks along the sea. Oysters are shellfish that parasitize on rocks and wooden pillars near the water. The chiselers wait for low tide and only need to use a piece of iron to chisel away the shells to get the oyster meat. However, some also chisel off the oysters along with their shells, put them in buckets, and carry them home to leisurely open the oyster shells.

The oyster meat that is dug out is milky white and has a texture as soft as cotton. It also tastes sweet and delicious. Because it has no blood, those who abstain from killing often take it as an aid to their meals, regarding it as the ultimate food.

(Note) The Chaoshan people often call "oyster omelette" "蚝劣" [háo liè]. The character "劣" [liè] is taken for its pronunciation. For convenience, I take its meaning and call it "蠔煎" [háo jiān - oyster omelette].

April Term Implemented 279

The gold exchange settlement price issue has been resolved at yesterday's meeting. The March contracts will be based on the British and American exchange rates, without hedging, and will be settled at the end of March. As for the April contracts (using the market weight), they will still be based on the US dollar settlement price. However, because the US dollar has already reduced its fineness, after calculation, starting from April, US$346 will be equal to one strip of bullion, starting from February 20th, the April term trading will begin (this is because a part of the hedgers bear the risks during the customs closure period, and there is a saying that the April trading should be started early during the Lunar New Year).

The Inevitability of Japanese Rice Dumping in China

The Japanese Government is Determined to Do it at a Loss 280

It is Difficult for China to Prevent It from Coming

Since the rumor that Japan intends to dump its surplus rice in China, the grain industry and government authorities in this city have paid attention to it and issued statements, believing that there may be no possibility of Japanese rice dumping in China. A reporter from this newspaper specially visited a gentleman who specializes in the study of people's food problems. According to his conversation and the statistics he presented on the import quantity and value of rice from Japan, Taiwan, and Korea, the dumping of Japanese rice in China may still be possible despite the low price of rice. The gentleman said,

"Since Japan implemented the Rice Control Law, it has already shown signs of being overstretched. Although human labor is said to be omnipotent, it still has many shortcomings when under severe pressure from nature. The most difficult aspects of the Rice Control Law are the setting of official prices and the maintenance of rice prices. The method of maintaining these prices is for the government to invest in purchasing rice. Regardless of what happens after the purchase, the government may not have this power at the time of purchase, and stopping abruptly may cause resentment among the people. Continuously buying up rice will eventually exhaust financial resources, so if Japan truly has a bumper harvest, it must find another way out. Otherwise, the Japanese government will also be difficult to be this large hoarder. According to the current situation, the Japanese parliament is asking questions like this, and the Japanese cabinet is anxiously seeking remedies. This surplus of ten million 石 [shí - approximately 180 liters] of rice, if stored in Japan, will have no good opportunity for Japanese rice. Rather than caring about the loss of this ten million 石 of surplus rice, and letting the rice price fall to a point where it cannot be maintained, causing peasant riots and the cabinet to collapse, it would be better to endure the pain and sacrifice, dispose of this ten million 石 of surplus rice clearly, so that Japanese farmers can rest and the Japanese government can also slightly relieve the pain of buying surplus rice.

The dumping of rice from Japan, Taiwan, and Korea in China has four routes. First, the three northeastern provinces occupied by the Japanese puppet regime. The three northeastern provinces sometimes rely on Korean rice for supply, and because the soil is connected and the Koreans and Manchus live together, it is common to adjust each other's surpluses and shortages. Now, under the occupation of the Japanese, the door is wide open, and dumping is not a problem. The second is Tianjin and other places in North China, because of the Japanese concessions, activities are naturally convenient. In recent years, the Tianjin merchant group has purchased a considerable amount of粳米 [jīng mǐ - Japonica rice] from Shanghai, which is an opportunity to promote Japanese rice. As for the Yangtze River area, it is a rice-producing area, and dumping is originally not easy, but our country has absolutely no statistics on rice production and sales, so whether the high or low price of rice today is a problem of rice itself, or whether the farmers' economy is bankrupt and they cannot store it and provide it all to the market, causing the price of rice to fall, if this is the case, then the low price of rice at the moment may have hope of returning to normal after February or March of this year. If the rice price is high, Japanese rice may take the opportunity to invade. At that time, the hub for its dumping will be Shanghai, where Japanese warships and ships gather. As for the two provinces of Fujian and Guangdong, they are the sales area for foreign rice, especially the areas of Quanzhou, Zhangzhou, and Fuzhou in Fujian, which are small in area and densely populated. Before Taiwan was ceded to Japan, Taiwanese rice was the only supply for Fujian province. After Taiwan was ceded to Japan, with the efforts of the Japanese to develop it, coupled with two harvests a year, rice production increased quite rapidly, far beyond what it was in the Qing dynasty. Even in the last ten years, the increase has been large. In 1924, it was 5.68 million 石, and by 1933, it had become 8.36 million 石. Japan also transplanted its own rice varieties to Taiwan to improve them, which is the so-called "蓬萊米 [péng lái mǐ - Ponlai rice]". Japan also regards Fujian as its sphere of influence, so the Japanese government's dumping of Taiwanese rice in Fujian and Guangdong is easy to handle and can be expected to succeed.

Judging from the above situation, except for the Yangtze River basin, which is difficult to win at the moment, South China and North China can be sure. Some say that the price of Japanese rice is high, and selling it in China will inevitably lead to losses. This view is correct in ordinary times, but not in extraordinary times. Japanese rice is currently in an extraordinary period. If surplus rice is not sold, there is no other way. Willingness to accept losses is already in the Japanese government's budget. Even if it is transported to the Yangtze River area and various commercial ports in North China, the losses will be borne by the Japanese government. The losses from dumping Taiwanese rice will be filled by the Taiwanese people and the Taiwanese government equally. Its determination to do it is already conceivable. Moreover, the reason why rice prices in Japan are higher than in China is also because its capacity is larger than ours. Our country now calculates in 公石 [gōng shí - hectoliters] (巿石 [shì shí - market 石] is the same amount). One 石 of Japanese rice is approximately equal to one hectoliter and eight 公斗 [gōng dǒu - decaliters] and a little more. Even if the Shanghai rice price is eight yuan per hectoliter, the price of one 石 of Japanese rice should be fourteen yuan and forty cents. At 112 合 [hé - combined with] Japanese currency, it is sixteen yuan and one dime and change. The quality of Japanese rice is also better than Japonica rice, so the high rice price in Shanghai means that Japanese rice has the possibility of dumping. Moreover, since it is said to be dumping, only selling is desired, and other things are not considered.

Some say that since foreign rice is taxed, foreign rice has long disappeared in Shanghai. Even if Japanese rice is imported, it will be difficult to compete with local rice. I don't know that Fujian and Guangdong provinces have long been excluded. Even if Fujian and Guangdong impose taxes and the Shanghai and Tianjin customs impose taxes, the Japanese can still use their special power to find ways to avoid it. Even if not, they will definitely be able to avoid the heavy and take the light. Don't you see that Japanese goods with very heavy tariffs can still be imported into China with their subtle transportation techniques and still dominate? Since the dumping of Japanese rice is presided over by the government, it will inevitably use all its strength to achieve it. Tariffs cannot prevent it from coming, how can the people resist its import? The arrival of Japanese rice is just around the corner. Let's see what happens later. (Table lengthy, omitted)

Extension of Silver and Money Industry Collection and Settlement Time

│Collection of Bills Until 4 PM│ 283

The silver and money industry's custom is that every lunar new year's end, they engage in summarizing the year's accounts. This time it is also the lunar year's end. All interactions with various parties must be summarized. Therefore, the procedures are vast, and the fixed period is insufficient for work. Therefore, it was decided that from yesterday (the 8th), the time would be extended. Bill collection ends at 4 PM, and organization ends at 10 PM. Therefore, all routine spare time settlement news, due to time constraints, cannot be calculated as usual. In the market, the interbank overnight rate remained at 2%, the same in the morning and afternoon. Clearing house transactions were initially white, then done at 2-3%. The total transaction volume was 11,013,000 yuan, including 3,000 yuan in spot goods, 3,785,000 in futures taxes, 1,100,000 in troop reduction bonds, 870,000 in 19 customs duty bonds, 1,715,000 in 20-volume 20-customs duty bonds, 1,360,000 in gold short-term bonds, and the rest ranged from tens of thousands to two or three hundred thousand.

New Fung Foreign Firm's 7th Report: The New York stock market declined, the first major reaction of 1934. Because of the continuous rise in recent days, the technical position was inevitably weak. Now that the bill to regulate the exchange is under discussion, the situation in France is uncertain, and many bulls are selling off in large quantities, the market has started to decline. Small speculators were forced to sell out completely. Utility stocks were hit the hardest, but gold and silver stocks remained firm throughout the day. Bonds were mixed and slightly weak. Looking at the recent situation, it may temporarily hover. The total daily transaction volume was 4.5 million shares. "Cotton" fell because it was rumored that the Punk-Hay Agreement would not be implemented this year, and many bulls closed their positions. People still had confidence in automatic acreage reduction. However, all transactions were price-limited, so the market was stable. As a result, February and March fell by 0.015 yuan, April fell by 0.0175 yuan, May and June fell by 0.02 yuan, and July fell by 0.0175 yuan.

The Flour Exchange will be closed for the Spring Festival holiday from today until the 18th. Trading will resume on the 19th, with only the morning market trading six rounds. Full-day business will resume from the 24th.

Silk and Tea

Overseas Silk Sales Have Undergone a Turnaround

(Wuxi Silk Factory Preparing to Resume Work) Wuxi has always been a famous silk-producing area in our country. There are a total of 50 silk factories in the entire county. For years, silk sales in Europe and America have been in a slump, and the silk industry has collapsed. All factories were closed before the lunar New Year's Eve last year. Since the beginning of the year, only six or seven factories have been working reluctantly. Now that overseas silk sales have gradually turned around, the closed factories are resuming work one after another. As of the day before yesterday, there were 12 silk factories in the entire county that had started work, including Yongtai, Jinji, Huaxin, and Zhenyi. More than a dozen other factories are preparing to continue starting work during the lunar New Year.

(Factory Raw Silk 63 Bales Shipped to Lake) The Huangbai factory raw silk purchased by various silk merchants in Shanghai in the Lake area is now being shipped back one after another to meet the needs of the machines. Yesterday, another 63 bales of white factory raw silk were shipped to Huxun.

(Factory Raw Silk Spot Silk Sales Still Smooth) As overseas silk sales are improving day by day, the domestic silk factories are still eager to buy Huangbai factory raw silk. The trend continues to take the opportunity to buy. Yesterday, various silk merchants from Hangzhou, Lake, and Shanghai continued to purchase 90 bales of Grade B Huangbai factory raw silk, and the price continued to rise.

Da Lai

Page 17

Free Talk Essays Heyezi

In recent years, it can be said that the era of essays is prevalent. Because of its prevalence, many people study it, and there are various conclusions. Of course, there are people who look down on it. Needless to say, they must be good at writing long essays. Wang Chong of the Han Dynasty wrote "Lunheng" in eighty-five chapters, which can be called a large book. The wording of each chapter is also very tight and rich. In his "Zi Ji," he said: "Few words without much, and no few gorgeous writings. Those that are used by the world, a hundred chapters are harmless; those that are not used, one chapter is useless. If all are used, then the more is superior, and the less is inferior. Accumulating a thousand gold is compared to one hundred, who is richer? It can be said that many articles are better than few, and few wealth becomes poorer. The world has no one volume, but I have a hundred chapters; people have no one word, but I have ten thousand words, who is the wiser?" These few words have already judged the merits of long essays and short essays. Today's critics can really quote them.

However, Wang Chong is speaking from the author's standpoint. All authors always like more works and longer articles, because this can prove the greatness of his talent and the depth of his knowledge, just like "accumulating a thousand gold" can show off wealth. However, in terms of purpose, wasting a thousand gold is not necessarily better than making good use of a hundred gold. Similarly, a long and verbose article is not necessarily better than a short essay. When a doctor bought a donkey, the contract was three pages long, but the word "donkey" was nowhere to be found, which was spread as a joke, which shows that long articles also have times when they are useless. And essays sometimes have great effects.

I can give an example. A few days ago, there was such a news item in the newspaper:

"Guangdong Province is unusually cold this winter. The harvest of sweet potatoes and other crops has been greatly damaged. On the roads, there are starving people without winter clothes, who feel great pain. Guangzhou has even had snowfall, which is a rare occurrence. Luofu Mountain now has several inches of accumulated snow, and the scenery is particularly beautiful."

Although this is only sixty or so words, it very clearly and naturally points out the contradictions of modern society: in the same winter, some people feel pain because they have no winter clothes, while others feel that the "scenery is particularly beautiful" because of the several inches of accumulated snow. At the same time, it also points out that a certain type of people in modern times have two souls, one soul that makes him see the suffering of the starving, and another soul that makes him turn around to appreciate the snow scene. But this is not an intentional propaganda by socialists, but merely a factual account by a journalist. He wrote these sixty or so words only to faithfully report a piece of news, not to intentionally criticize society. However, unintentionally, the truth of this society was clearly exposed by him.

If a great writer with great talent were to write a long and verbose article of ten thousand words about the injustices of modern society, I think the effect on the reader would not necessarily be greater than those sixty or so words. Moreover, we often see many articles that, because they have to be long, say this and that in a roundabout way, but unconsciously say things that contradict each other, making it impossible for the reader to see what is going on.

Therefore, I think that the quality of an article really has nothing to do with its length. Wang Chong's words should be changed to "Those that are used by the world, one chapter is harmless. Those that are not used, a hundred chapters are useless."

Is Tao Gong a Farmer? Guyun

I casually talked about Tao Yuanming last time because I read an article by Mr. Cao Juren. Yesterday I read Free Talk on February 5th, and I was honored by Mr. Cao's reply and was rudely referred to as a member of the "Tao Party". Junfang's language is wonderful in the world, and I can't help but fear that it will hinder the handsome. I am very grateful for Mr. Cao's meaning. Whenever something raises a question, it must be proven by supporting evidence. Tao Gong has been dead for many years. Mr. Cao said that he "does not associate with farmers": and I said that he is a "farmer who can write poetry". To determine this case, we must "throw the book bag". But my book box is all in the north. I am ashamed to say that I don't have a single book in my Shanghai residence. If I want to run to a very far library to search, I had this "phlegm" ten years ago, but now my spine has been broken by life, and I am no longer allowed to be so elegant. Today, I borrowed three incomplete collections of Tao's works from a friend and wrote this first draft to consult Mr. Cao. I am afraid there are many mistakes. Because I have no books at hand, it is like having no weapons in the army, and I dare not fight this battle. If I can throw a brick to attract jade because of my humble words, and another learned gentleman is willing to talk about it, then I will shrink back and consider it a special honor.

Now, I will interpret Mr. Cao's reply and express my extended words:

I slightly quoted Tao's poems in my previous article as evidence that Tao Gong cultivated the land himself. Mr. Cao answered in his article by discussing the world and knowing people, talking about the social chaos of the Eastern Jin Dynasty and the desolation of the countryside, and deeply wondered why Tao's poems ignored the dark shadows of the countryside. That's right. But this cannot be used to prove that Tao was not a farmer. The dark shadows of the Chinese countryside are even worse than those of the Eastern Jin Dynasty. Almost all of today's farmers do not understand the countryside. However, they are still farmers even if they become farmers. What distinguishes Tao Gong from ordinary farmers is that he is a farmer who is a Confucian poet. He is a person who only cares about his own moral cultivation. It is true that he ignores the widespread dark shadows of the countryside. Because besides Confucian thought, everything else about him is the same as ordinary farmers. He did not open his eyes to make a general expression of the countryside. But the poverty and hardship he described in his poems and articles are precisely a concrete corner of the countryside, which is not inconsistent with Mr. Cao's discussion.

Regarding Tao's drinking and traveling, I said in my previous article that they were rest after labor.

His dream of the Peach Blossom Spring is enough to explain him. "They go back and forth to plant and cultivate, and the clothes of men and women are all like those of outsiders. Old people with white hair and children with their hair in tufts are all happily enjoying themselves... They say that their ancestors fled from the chaos of the Qin Dynasty and led their wives, children, and villagers to this isolated place."

"Mulberry trees and bamboos cast their remaining shadows, and soybeans and millet are planted in season. Spring silkworms gather long silk, and the autumn harvest is exempt from royal taxes." This is Tao's "ivory tower". And I secretly believe that this is precisely a painful reflection of a good farmer under the harsh government in troubled times. After the pain, he dreamed of this "isolated place" that was "exempt from royal taxes". Tao Gong never lived in the "ivory tower" for a single day in his life.

Mr. Cao mentioned at the end of his article that the people of Wuhan were fish the year before last, and some people were floating in boats on moonlit nights, flirting with prostitutes and singing songs. His words are extremely painful. Mr. Cao made this statement because he was moved by this world. My sadness and Mr. Cao's are exactly the same. And I believe that if Tao Gong were still alive, he would definitely hate it deeply. Because Tao Gong suffered more than Mr. Cao and I. There is no exception to what Tao feels for what we are saddened about.

Now, please follow the root. Was Tao Yuanming a farmer after all?

Of course, Tao Yuanming was not a farmer from birth, but he made up his mind to "transform" (please forgive me for using this fashionable word) into a farmer after he resigned from his post. He remained so until his death.昭明序陶集 has "...贞志不休，安道苦节。不以躬耕为耻，不以无财为病"之言，而其为陶作传亦云，“……亲老家贫，起为州祭酒。不堪吏职，少日自解归。州召主簿，不就。躬耕自资，遂抱赢疾……"顏延年靖節徵士誄 has "...於是乎遂灌畦鬻蔬，爲供魚菽之祭；織絇緯蕭，以充糧粒之費". However, these words from others can only be used as collateral evidence.

Let's seek direct evidence from Tao Gong himself.祭從弟敬遠文 has "…每忆有秋，我将其刈。"自祭文 has "自余为人，逢运之贫。箪瓢屡罄，絺綌冬陈。含欢谷汲，行歌负薪。翳翳柴门，事我宵晨。春秋代谢，有务中园。载耘载耔，乃育廼繁。欣以素牍，和以七絃。冬曝其日，夏濯其泉。勤靡余劳心有长闲" "有会而作" has "旧谷既没，新谷未登。颇为老农，而值年灾。日月尚悠，为患未已。…" These are all portrayals of his own life. In his poem "Diligent Farming," he cites Shun, Yu, Ji Que, Ju Ni, and other sages who still cultivated the land themselves, and tells everyone not to "drag their robes and stand with their hands clasped." He tells everyone to be diligent and not to enjoy ease. This can be regarded as his theory.归田园居 has "…种苗在东 畴，苗生满阡陌。虽有荷锄倦，浊酒聊自适" and刘柴桑 has "…茅茨已就治，新畴复应畬。" Let's look at the titles of two more poems: one is "Gengxu Year, Ninth Month, Harvesting Armor in the West Field," and the other is "Bingchen Year, Eighth Month, Harvesting in the Lower Xun Field House." These two poems further detail his own hard work in farming, and a kind of joy of diligent harvest is not easy to imitate. This is the realization of his theory.

The correct words have been spoken. Please go one step further and ask why Tao Gong, as a farmer, ate so much bitterness and was a man of outstanding thought, ignored the dark shadows of the rural areas at that time? I said in the previous article that Tao Gong used Confucian thought. There are many categories of Confucianism. Tao Gong used the most basic narrow road of Confucianism. Liang Rengong once argued that Tao Gong was a kind of person that Confucius called "robbers". In his later years, his meritorious deeds were fulfilled and he had the joy of self-satisfaction. (I remember that Liang's book "Tao Yuanming" published by the Commercial Press had this saying.) I sympathize with Rengong's statement. He is the most upright person. The characteristic of this kind of person is that the scope is often not easy to broaden. He is poor and works hard. Tan Daoji sent him Liang Rou, even when he was hungry and upset, he would not bother to take a look. Yan Yanzhi is an old friend and sent him 20,000 yuan. Okay, accept it. You can take it to buy wine and have fun. But he will never take it to use as his own. Among the dirty gentry at that time, he stubbornly acted as an iron man who did not follow the customs and only cared about his own moral cultivation. In order to achieve this goal of personal independence │ what he himself said he did not ask for │ he used farming as a means to achieve this goal. He broke through all the sieges of hunger, cold, and hardship, and finally he gained the pleasure of personal independence. He devoted all his energy to this. Therefore, he is ultimately a person who only cares about his own moral cultivation. Therefore, it is not surprising that he ignores the general rural phenomena.

Whether people in the present era still want to be a person exactly like Yuanming is another question. Most people with clear minds are probably unwilling to advocate a person who is exactly like Tao. We return Tao Yuanming to Tao Yuanming, then Yuanming seems to be like this.

Finally, thank you Mr. Cao for your kind reply!

In Singapore

Black Baby Singapore! Paris on the Equator.

I jumped ashore, raised my head, and a skyscraper stood before my eyes. I looked up layer by layer along the honeycomb-like windows; the flag of the Great British Empire was inserted on the top of the skyscraper!

Trolleybuses, cars, motorcycles, ... came and went horizontally and vertically, echoing metallic noises in my ears.

Rickshaw pullers were shouting. -- These poor rickshaw pullers who have been forgotten by the motherland! Wearing tattered hats, half-naked, sweat pouring straight down their foreheads, their skin aching from the scorching sun: but who cares?

Indian police officers were waving wooden sticks behind them. Rickshaw pullers are often beaten: in people's eyes, they seem to no longer be human beings.

The Ningbo people who raised the "T"-shaped hoes were all black and panting. They hoed the asphalt road again and again. The cars brushed past them, whooshing, and a burst of thick smoke sprayed out from their butts, with a smell of oil.

I was pulled by a rickshaw to live in "Nantian". In the desert-like equator, Singapore really cannot but be regarded as Paris. Look!

Skyscrapers. The magnificent General Post Office. Banks. ...

The famous Oriental cinema Capital. New World Amusement Park. Nantian Grand Restaurant. ...

Imperialism has invaded here for quite some time. The black smoke from the factories rises straight up all day long. However, with the economic panic becoming more and more severe, Singapore naturally has no way to prosper.

I saw so many empty shops, so many unemployed workers. I also saw Indian police officers grabbing petty thieves and beating them. At night, when the lights of the New World are shining brightly, there are countless hungry people suffering from hunger and cold in front of the doors of empty shops. They have no warm quilts, no money, no home! ...

God, what can I say?

I'm just a passerby!

Dance halls have also been opened in Singapore. Society is contradictory after all; on the one hand, some people are starving, while on the other hand, some people are drinking champagne and dancing.

"Who cares, I'll go dancing while I still have money today!"

A friend of mine said that.

So the revelry of jazz music leaked faintly from the magnificent dance hall, and two or three beggars were waiting anxiously outside the door. When the gentlemen came, they chased after them:

"Do a good deed..."

Before they could finish speaking, they had already run inside.

I wandered around here for a while and finally left.

I left Singapore on a drizzly evening. With a whoosh, the ship moved step by step. I was alone on the deck, looking at the dense lights, the shadows of the skyscrapers, as if thousands of sharp arrows were inserted into my heart.

I couldn't say a word.

I'm just a passerby!

I Curse That Smile of Yours (2) Wu Yan

"Going to the barbarian land? That's dangerous, no one will come back."

Naturally, I had to get to the bottom of the matter, and the answer was:

"Why do you say that? You'll be caught by the women there!"

The meaning is that in the area bordering Myanmar and Siam, there are some barbarians whose women are more beautiful than Han Chinese girls and are more likely to tempt people. Although the words are a bit too much, the meaning is partly correct.

These Yi women who come down to the valley to spend the night mostly -- it seems almost as a rule -- come to our shop first. Only when it's really full do they go to Old Liu's shop. Few go to the other shops. This is not because our inn treats guests with special humility or charges less. The reason is that the proprietress of our shop and her eldest daughter can both speak three languages, and can be said to be the two linguistic giants in this small valley. The proprietress learned the local savage language here, and at the same time, because she was born to a Han Chinese father and an Yi mother, she was naturally very proficient in both Han Chinese and Yi languages. Her eldest daughter, on the other hand, should be regarded as her mother's proud disciple in the course of linguistics. Therefore, those Yi women who come from afar are happy to come and stay overnight for the convenience of speaking and also to get the friendly greetings of the female owner of the same ethnic group.

As for Old Liu's shop, his woman is a savage woman who can speak some Yi language, but is not very proficient. However, compared to those inns where no one understands even Yi language, she can be regarded as a diplomatic talent, without being deficient in any way. Therefore, the Yi people who cannot stay in our shop are also willing to stay overnight.

The owners of other inns, because they lack this kind of diplomatic linguistic talent, their business is naturally much inferior, and they often scratch their heads and express such envious words to these two shops, especially our shop:

"Well, it would be great if I had such a wife!"

"Even half would be fine, ... like Old Liu's!"

My boss, on the other hand, is also very complacent, thinking that with such a wife as the foreign minister and such a daughter as the assistant, he can simply be called king in this small valley. No matter what country's envoys (travelers of various races) come to pay tribute (stay overnight) and offer tribute (pay the bill), he does not feel any diplomatic difficulties at all.

But once, a guest who came to buy goods actually caused a bit of an interesting incident in diplomacy because of the language communication.

Could it be that the person who came was a deaf-mute person? No, he is still proficient in three languages. Don't you think this is very interesting?

This person also lives in the valley, and specializes in managing the construction of roads in the mountains. If a section of the mountain road is suddenly washed away by a mountain flood, and the camel and horse caravans going from Bamou to Tengyue cannot pass, then the British authorities in Bamou will send someone to investigate and blame him. He is an Indian who understands Burmese and English. But when he calls on the savages to come down the mountain to repair the road, he must first find a savage who can speak Burmese to be the foreman.

Shenbao Local Supplement: Talk About Shanghai Qiongsheng

At the end of 1929, due to the bankruptcy of the New York Stock Exchange, the world economic crisis that erupted quickly stirred up the entire world. Wherever it reached, industrial and commercial closures, bank bankruptcies, rural economic destruction, and the deterioration of the lives of the working class and farmers, unemployment and starvation became inevitable and already occurring phenomena. Considering the situation in our country in recent years, the "decline of all industries" and "rural bankruptcy" have long been problems that people in power, politicians, and economists have been anxious about and unable to solve. Worker unemployment, farmer crop failures and disasters, and even bumper harvests become disasters. As a result, banditry prevails and society is in turmoil. All of these are due in part to the world economic crisis, which seems to be an "undeniable" fact. However, in the wave of China's overall economic bankruptcy years ago, Shanghai was the only port that could stand alone and create a new situation. Under the coercion of "recession," it still maintained "prosperity," which was truly unique. Indeed, Shanghai's population growth, the construction of many large buildings, the development of the banking industry, the sharp rise in land prices, and the increase in rents all seem to indicate the prosperity of this "international market" and show signs of great "prosperity." This phenomenon of "prosperity" has made some people who have made money in the interior, "with ten million strings of cash around their waists, riding cranes to Yangzhou," come to this "ten-mile foreign market" as "retired gentlemen." Amidst the cries of ruin and desolation, supplemented by the joyful voices of "Shanghai's prosperity," it has also led many romantic and optimistic gentlemen, regardless of how the world is feeling the shock of the "crisis," to forget themselves and make countless "Greater Shanghai Construction Plans" and "work hard" to build "Greater Shanghai."

However, this cheer of "Shanghai's prosperity" is more悲傷 to me than hearing the funeral song of the pastor sending the dead to the grave, and this effort to build "Greater Shanghai" is more心痛 than seeing the gravedigger working hard to bury the carcass that has lost its "soul." Shanghai's prosperity, instead of being praised as the development of China's industry and commerce, should be said to be the collection of the blood shed by the people of the whole country for several years. Instead of considering it as the "consolidation" of China's financial economy, it is better to regard it as the expansion of the suction tube of imperialism that squeezes the blood and sweat of the Chinese people. Because after the world economic crisis swept China, Shanghai was still able to maintain its "prosperity" on the surface, not because Shanghai, this "economic center," was able to turn the tide and become a "pillar in the torrent," but in reality, it contained the following three meanings:

First, the world economic crisis caused by the existence of the world capitalist system has made the excess products and surplus capital of various powers, under the situation where imperialists and their vassals are shouting "closed-door economy" and "economic war" and implementing "tariff barriers," have nowhere to sell and nowhere to invest before using a big war to "redivide the world." Of course, our country, with its "open door and equal opportunity," has become a target for dumping foreign goods and foreign capital. And Shanghai, this gateway to the coast and the interior and the "metropolis of the East," has become the focus of various countries' invasion of the Chinese market. This kind of "prosperity" is undoubtedly the tomb of China's industry and the consolidation of imperialist power.

Second, years of civil war and natural and man-made disasters, after "destroying" the "production" of the rural economy, drove many wealthy families and hungry groups from the countryside to the city to seek a happy land and find work. Therefore, Shanghai's "prosperity" has only increased many "retired gentlemen," resulting in higher rents, sharp rises in land prices, and countless unemployed, idlers, bandits, and beggars. This kind of "prosperity" is a reflection of China's economic bankruptcy and the people's poverty.

Third, the construction of the so-called "Greater Shanghai Plan," in addition to the fact that this "strong outside and weak inside" "prosperity" will inevitably turn it into a fantasy, will undoubtedly only create speculators such as real estate tycoons and landlords who are of no help to industry, and "work hard" to consolidate the "international market" of the powers.

However, no matter how the "Greater Shanghai Construction Plan" "works hard," after a period of "prosperity," the cry of "the decline of Greater Shanghai" has now begun. According to recent reports, "This port is not only the largest commercial market in the Far East, but also the political, economic, industrial, and commercial center of the country. For years, various places have been plagued by civil wars and natural and man-made disasters... Only Shanghai has not been affected... Only in recent years, due to the intrusion of foreign goods, the domestic economy has been exhausted, and recently the recession has become more severe, with imports exceeding 700 million." After this painful narrative, it is described that at the end of the lunar year, there is a rumor that 500 large businesses have gone bankrupt, and Nanjing Road, which is similar to the Tokyo Ginza and New York Wall Street, has more than 50% of its stores in debt. The Shanghai Special District Local Court has received more than half of the lawsuits accusing Nanjing Road merchants, and the seals cannot be issued according to legal procedures. This fact is where Shanghai's "prosperity" lies, and also where the "Greater Shanghai Plan" lies! "The decline of Greater Shanghai," "the decline of Greater Shanghai." If anyone has unspeakable feelings of nostalgia and cherishing the old for this "decline" caused by an unsound system, there is no way but to offer condolences to him.

Mother and Son Boer

It's a pity that his little soul lives with his young mother in the severe cold and snow.

"Living is really not easy, and you still want to cry!" His mother said in a deep and resentful voice.

"Aiyo... Aiyo... Aiyo" The child, who was not yet two years old, did not understand his mother's depression, and he cried and cried. His mother knew that he was hungry, but what could she do to make him stop crying and not be hungry? She got up at six o'clock in the morning and ran around until now. Everyone else had eaten their lunch, and she had only borrowed two small coins from Mingyou. No wonder he was crying. The mother had to comfort him and say, "You little animal, go to sleep. When you wake up, you'll have food to eat!" He cried so tired that he fell asleep in his mother's arms. The mother did not dare to put him on the bed, fearing that he would be cold and also fearing that he would wake up. So, she held him with one hand and cooked with the other. In such cold weather, she closed the door and lit the most economical coal briquette stove in Shanghai, which could cook food and at the same time let the child get some warmth.

The mother thought he must be sleeping very comfortably, but who knew that he suddenly jumped up from her arms, and the tone of his crying was different from usual, as if he was frightened. She thought the child might be having a nightmare and patiently patted him to go back to sleep. Before the rice was cooked, he had cried like this several times. His hands and feet were constantly dancing, and the mother was very impatient. She thought he would be quiet if she gave him food, but who knew that this time it was not like this. He did not want to eat, he wanted to cry, wanted to jump up and sit up, but he also wanted to go to sleep. He could not settle down and was very tired. His vermilion lips suddenly turned as white as snow at this time. She saw that this situation was not good, so she picked him up and paced around the room, rocking him and singing to him. In an instant, she did not know what was going on, but she felt as if she could not stand up, her feet were soft, her head was heavy, her eyes were blurry, and she felt like she was going
